  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1968676049" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1968676049?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1968676049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15897441204402133475"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"There is a hole in your heart, an empty space. You must fill it with <i>meaning</i>. You need a cause to live for, to fight for, perhaps to die for... Choose me."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><b>
  <u>4.5 Stars:✰✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br/><br/>Just a warning, this is less of a review and more of me explaining why this book was so personally meaningful to me. If you hate that stuff, please move on ;] haha. I almost feel like this book could have been written just for me, and very, VERY few books have ever done that. <b>Simply fantastic opening to what I'm</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15897441204402133475" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"There is a hole in your heart, an empty space. You must fill it with <i>meaning</i>. You need a cause to live for, to fight for, perhaps to die for... Choose me."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><b>
  <u>4.5 Stars:✰✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br /><br />Just a warning, this is less of a review and more of me explaining why this book was so personally meaningful to me. If you hate that stuff, please move on ;] haha. I almost feel like this book could have been written just for me, and very, VERY few books have ever done that. <b>Simply fantastic opening to what I'm predicting will wind up being listed among my all time favorite series.</b> <br /><br />I don't even know where to begin, if I'm being completely honest. I can't figure out exactly how to put what I want to get across into words. So many different elements about the characters and the story in this book just <b>
  <i>resonated</i>
</b> with me on a very deep level. I could see glimpses of myself in each of these characters, and not because of their strengths. I see myself in them because of their struggles. <br /><br />Gonna get a little bit real here for a second. I don't like doing this in my reviews, but I can't really talk about why I loved this book without talking a little bit about my own life. A lot like Corban, I feel like most of my life when I was younger was spent living under anger and fear. Or else, living under fear disguised as anger. <i>Unlike</i> Corban though, I wasn't this naturally likeable or well-intentioned kid. I was more like the Rafe of this story, and if that makes me sound awful, it's because I actually was pretty awful. I was bitter, and spiteful, and angry at everybody - all the time - and I didn't even know why. I was insecure, and I hated myself, and I took it out on other people. This turned into self-pity. Which turned into a deep-rooted selfishness. Which eventually turned into shame. I lost the few friends that I had because I pushed them away. I pushed away my siblings and my parents and never let anybody in. <br /><br />In short, <b>my life was ruled by my feelings of anger and fear and insecurity, and I never, ever fought back</b>. For me, becoming the person that I am today looked like me learning to fight and conquer my own feelings. Bravery didn't look like me picking up a sword and fighting giants. Courage was not me standing up to the bullies that were picking on me. It looked like me learning how to fight the giants that existed in my own mind, to the death. It looked like me learning how to actually receive the love of my family and friends, and learning to give that same love in return. It was the hardest thing I've ever had to do. And even though it took several years, it started with me saying these simple words to myself - this is a direct quote from the book: <br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Fear will not rule me."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />I read these words in chapter 3 of this book, and instantly knew that this book was for me: <br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"We all fear, Ban. Even Tull. It's what we do about it-that's the important thing. That's what'll make you the man you grow into. You must learn to control your emotions, boy. Those that don't do that often end up dead: anger, fear, pride, whatever. If your emotions control you, sooner or later you're a dead man... Learn to control them and they can be a tool that makes you stronger."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />I wish somebody told me this when I was younger, and I can't tell you how happy it makes me that people are writing stories that deal with themes like this. Stories that don't just deal with battles and action and war, but <b>also deal with the wars that so often occur in the heart of every human being.</b> People tell me that I look like a completely different person compared to who I used to be, and it's because I learned these truths. Most of the battles we fight as people take place within ourselves.<br /><br />You'll hear people talk about the number of POVs in this book, and <b>yes, there are an almost overwhelming number of POVs in this book</b>. But I can tell you for certain that what John Gwynne accomplished with each member of this cast of characters, most authors can never accomplish with even a single POV. The level of wisdom, leadership understanding, and even basic conception of human nature that Gwynne displays in this book blew my mind. I felt like he understood me, just from reading about these characters. Seriously amazing character development, for both the good guys and the bad guys. <br /><br />The simplistic worldbuilding is still excellently done. While this is not Sanderson-level originality, Gwynne sticks to where his strengths lie, and this works in his favor. This world has a very medieval vibe to it, and the writing had a certain feel to it that very obviously shows that Gwynne has deep knowledge of the things he writes about. <b>Seriously, he knows his stuff</b>. You know how a lot of authors, rather than fully describing a sword fight or battle scene, will just vaguely write about it and leave you to fill in the gaps in your imagination? (This was an issue I had with Michael Sullivan's books). <b>That won't happen in this book</b>. Clearly, Gwynne understands swordplay and battle tactics on a very detailed level, and this truly immerses you in the action of the story, when you aren't focused on the great characters. <br /><br />Lastly, the story. The presentation of the story is a very slow burn, but still really, really good. It took me awhile to figure out exactly what the drive of the plot was for the book as a whole, as Gwynne spends a lot of time acquainting you with the individual struggles of the characters before you figure out the world as a whole. For some, this will be a turn off, but for me it worked really well. I have a feeling we are going to have a much faster paced story in book two, but regardless, this book was truly excellent all on it's own. I much prefer a character-driven story over the various alternatives. <br /><br />My only complaint is that there is a definite learning curve required, in reference to the writing. Lots of "huh" and "eh" grunts that seemed weirdly placed to me, and some of the sentences were structured rather oddly. I got used to it very quickly, but it did turn me off a little bit at the beginning. If you pick it up just keep that in mind when you're reading that it might take a little getting used to =]. <br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Both the brave man and the coward feel the same. The only difference between them is that the brave man faces his fear, does not run."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Seriously - no, seriously. Read this book</b>. Depending on who you are, it might require more patience than another book would, as the beginning moves very slowly at the start. It is worth the time you spend on it though. For me, this book went beyond just being a "good book", because it touched on several themes that I've had to learn and wrestle with in my own life. That doesn't happen often. Beyond that though, this book has an amazing cast of characters, brilliantly presented action with plenty of brutal realism, and a great story. I cannot recommend it enough. <br /><br />Happy reading =]. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Corban knew, beyond all measure of doubt, that from this moment things would never be the same again. His life had just changed irrevocably and forever."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15897441204402133475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1966264781?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      Craig

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1966264781" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16995314957152961395">A great BR with three swordsmen, who where with me in warrior trial and sat the Long Night: <b>Samir, Terry and Jokoloyo</b>. <br/><br/>When I first read a couple of reviews for “Malice”, I wasn’t sure if I want to try it. Mostly there were good reviews, but also I spotted some DNFs. So when <b>Craig</b> recommended this book and series to me, I thought I needed backup! Thank you guys for being there for me ❤ <br/><br/>"Malice” is an interesting story, about how good fights evil. I found values that make “Malice” a great read: l</span>
  <span id="freeText16995314957152961395" style="display:none">A great BR with three swordsmen, who where with me in warrior trial and sat the Long Night: <b>Samir, Terry and Jokoloyo</b>. <br><br>When I first read a couple of reviews for “Malice”, I wasn’t sure if I want to try it. Mostly there were good reviews, but also I spotted some DNFs. So when <b>Craig</b> recommended this book and series to me, I thought I needed backup! Thank you guys for being there for me ❤ <br><br>"Malice” is an interesting story, about how good fights evil. I found values that make “Malice” a great read: life-changing battles, heroes, heroines, a bit of magic, heart-breaking betrayals and over-whelming love. Not forgetting the characters, some of whom I fell in love with, or hate a lot. It’s all there, you just need to open the book ;)<br><br>Characters. I remember I had difficulty with a big cast when I read Malazan. At first I had this problem with “Malice”, too. This book really needs a cast list! It was difficult sometimes to catch who’s who as the story “happened” in several places/kingdoms and there were multiple characters. It was a great help that each chapter was named by the name of the character, who played the main role in it. <br><br>The story is told using several POVs, but from the very start I could single out a couple of them who were the core of the story. One of them was Ban. Ban is quite an ordinary guy, not so successful, but having great wishes :) I loved following him through the start of his life journey. His bond with Storm, oh my goodness, I was in awe ❤<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493020688ra/22575739.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also I loved Kastell and Maquin, they had a really great bromance! At first I liked Veradis, his honorable and faithful personality charmed me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, but as he went further, I just got disappointed with him :S I just thought: Wtf, ok, you are a good-hearted fellow and you keep following an obvious baddie for a really long time without suspecting?! Come on :S <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>I loved Cywen as she’s a character I look for in all books with kickass heroines ❤<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493020688ra/22575740.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Oh and thank you, Mr Gwynne for a special unit of kickass women! Hope to see them more! :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493020688i/22575741._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fighting was a peculiar matter in “Malice” for me. I missed detailed fights, like it was in Greatcoats, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some fights as with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[wyrms or giants <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were simply described and felt like an easy battle. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Fights with the loss of some good characters were done better. I liked the fact that people, who weren’t very skilled in fights, could change the course of a battle. That and the imprints of chivalry which thrived in the story :) <br><br>I‘m a bit disappointed as the „secret“ of Nate being <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[special and a traitor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was thin, I had suspicion from the first third of the book. On the other hand, the secrecy of Meical, Gar and some baddies was really well done. Oh and cheers for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Calidus and Rhin <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> as they were the villains I enjoyed having to pester Malice :)<br><br>The moral drama of the characters was peculiar and I was interested at first to see what’s behind the prophecy of the great good and the evil bad. But as I said before, it can be guessed quite early and well, it ripped quite a big chunk of joy out of me. Jealousy is the great motivator there, which gave me such an intriguing chance to see how simple childhood peer pressure can grow into dangerous life threats, despite the roots of honor and justice! <br><br><br>Narrative. I had struggle to get into the story for the half of the book. The pace often felt slow and to tell the truth I go distracted from reading. Putting this aside, I felt that the world in “Malice” was interestingly written, I could imagine the places and most of the characters felt real. The themes of betrayal, political scheming were quite well developed in the story. Though, I wanted a bit more of cool magic. Especially from the baddies! What really did the deed for me and gave joy and of course a bit of sadness, is the ending. OMG, it really blew my mind! <br><br>Despite all my ranting, “Malice” is a good book: I liked the Viking alike environment, scheming, most of the fighting, most of the character were well written and interesting to follow. I know that it’s the first book for Mr. Gwynne and I already heard that other books in this series are really more gripping, so I’ll continue my playdate with The Faithful and The Fallen for sure. <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3192026334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3192026334" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3192026334?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316399739" href="/book/show/17446626-malice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=recommendations">recommendations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3192026334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2237018955273292618"> <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/08/11/malice-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Come, boy, it is time for a lesson. Let me teach you the power of words,”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>I have heard tons of great things about this series and I have been putting reading it off for a long time because I am intimidated by huge books and this is a series of huge books. I also thought it would have more rigid writing and it would be hard to follow but I am glad I was wrong. This book was a great introduction to what I would expect to be an amazing series</span>
  <span id="freeText2237018955273292618" style="display:none"> <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/08/11/malice-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Come, boy, it is time for a lesson. Let me teach you the power of words,”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />I have heard tons of great things about this series and I have been putting reading it off for a long time because I am intimidated by huge books and this is a series of huge books. I also thought it would have more rigid writing and it would be hard to follow but I am glad I was wrong. This book was a great introduction to what I would expect to be an amazing series. I broke the fear of facing this series so I should be making my way through the rest of the series soon.<br /><br />John’s prose really took me by surprise, I finished the whole book in less than 4 days and I enjoyed what I was reading. It was hard to grab everything from the start, so I was making slow but steady progress and taking notes at the beginning but after like 20-25% of the book, it was much more easier to read and it made more sense. John’s writing is lush and I like the way he described things.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“The mountains were gone, replaced by a lush green vale. A river flowed out of the mountains, twisting in great curves through the vale until it”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />The Characters are well written too and although I am someone who enjoys multiple POVs, I think it is a tricky thing to write and read; write because you have to make every character distinct and interesting and read because you have to follow up with more than one character. I think the author managed to hit a good balance here, and although there was a lot to take at first, whether it is world-building, characters, magic..etc, It got better the more I progressed. Corban was definitely a character I rooted for and his animal companions were the best!<br /><br />The world-building is good too, the map definitely helps too. Regarding the magic system, it is not extensive in book 1 yet but I think it has much potential. I didn’t expect the book to have magical creatures to be honest, I thought it would be more like a historical fantasy focusing on politics but I was once again wrong.<br /><br />The plot is not very original in terms of classic epic fantasy plots. But John proved that you can still play with the classical tropes and make a great thing out of them. The plot we are exposed to seems like a drop of water in a sea that is the rest of the series. I think all the elements were done well with the potential to be even more epic.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Both the brave man and the coward feel the same. The only difference between them is that the brave man faces his fear, does not run.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>Summary:</b> I believe Malice is a book that sets things for something wider in scope and something more epic. Many elements of the story took me by surprise and were better than I expected. I already bought the rest of the series and I will be continuing the series soon!<br /><br />You can get more books from <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a><br /><br /><br />Awesome recommendation from my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52846007-nils-nilsreviewsit" rel="nofollow noopener">Nils</a> for my 10 readers, 10 recommendations challenge!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2237018955273292618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1660679697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1660679697" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1660679697?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660679697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8868798794062795084">4.5 stars.<br/>Normally I like to leave some space between books in a series, but with this one, I feel I need to continue quite quickly. Let me explain: this was one hard book to get into- so many names, I kept losing track. I was also listening on audio and the narrator was using everything from a Liverpudlian, Irish, scouser, Australian and Bavarian accents and they were distracting! I wouldn't recommend starting this book on audio until you have all the characters clear in your head.<br/>Having said t</span>
  <span id="freeText8868798794062795084" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br />Normally I like to leave some space between books in a series, but with this one, I feel I need to continue quite quickly. Let me explain: this was one hard book to get into- so many names, I kept losing track. I was also listening on audio and the narrator was using everything from a Liverpudlian, Irish, scouser, Australian and Bavarian accents and they were distracting! I wouldn't recommend starting this book on audio until you have all the characters clear in your head.<br />Having said that, this was a slow boiler and once the main characters were established, the story came together. Giants and wyrms, draigs, the obligatory megalomaniac baddy. There was nothing terribly original here- a coming of age story but I liked many of the characters particularly Corban and Cerwyn and Thannon, Gar, Shield, Storm and Craff, Brinn. It was a story well told and left almost in the midst of the action where sides have more or less been declared, where all the betrayers and double crossers have made their plays and where the rest of the series has been set up.<br />A thumping good read but give it til about 25% to get going!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8868798794062795084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1919063442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919063442" />
    <a title="Haïfa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa"><img alt="Haïfa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592921740p2/54721988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919063442?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haïfa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haïfa" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa">Haïfa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16300835-malice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919063442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17522848303727872309"><b>4.5 Scottish stars!<br/><br/>Buddy read with my favorite warriors : </b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/59458347-petrik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Petrik</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste' rel='nofollow noopener'>Celeste</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary</a> and my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/53385361-luna' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evil Twin</a> lurking in the shadows !<br/><br/><b>
  <u> Actual review </u>
</b><br/><br/>With his debut (!!!) novel, John Gwynne has just joined my list of authors who reaaally know how to write an ending (along with Brandon Sanderson and Mark Lawrence among others)!! The man knows how to grip his readers and wrap things up at the end to give a really satisfying conclusion and yet letting all the doors open to numerous unpredictable possibilitie</span>
  <span id="freeText17522848303727872309" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Scottish stars!<br><br>Buddy read with my favorite warriors : </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/59458347-petrik" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a> and my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/53385361-luna" rel="nofollow noopener">Evil Twin</a> lurking in the shadows !<br><br><b>
  <u> Actual review </u>
</b><br><br>With his debut (!!!) novel, John Gwynne has just joined my list of authors who reaaally know how to write an ending (along with Brandon Sanderson and Mark Lawrence among others)!! The man knows how to grip his readers and wrap things up at the end to give a really satisfying conclusion and yet letting all the doors open to numerous unpredictable possibilities. <b>The second half of the book was absolutely brilliant !</b> I was so enthralled and so anxious, sleep eluded me and I couldn't drop the book during the last quarter!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488335456ra/22102831.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The world created by Gwynne was quite detailed, with various kingdoms introduced. While the book <b>lacked ethnic diversity</b>, which I grew to like in Fantasy (the Stormlight Archive or Lightbringer series for example), <b>the mythology and lore are quite rich and well explained</b> throughout the narrative. Something I loved about the worldbuilding, is that most of the kingdoms shared the warrior customs and I really enjoyed reading about the training and the trials. John Gwynne introduced <b>a fair number of Fantasy elements in this debut</b>: giants, great beasts and monsters, magic, warring gods, epic battles, prophecies, chosen ones and coming of age storyline. But this book is also a tale of betrayal, of revenge, of loyalty, of deception and of courage. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I shall stay and tell my tale, hope that it may serve some purpose, that eyes shall see it and learn, that the future will not repeat the mistakes of the past. That is my prayer, but what use is prayer to a god that has abandoned all things . . .</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I won't lie and say that I loved the book from the beginning! Far from it actually! True, I enjoyed the read since the early pages but I couldn't understand all the praise the book got. <b>The first quarter was terribly slow</b>. Countless names and places were thrown at you and it was really hard to grasp all this information at once. It seemed that nothing really happened for the first 20% or 30% and some of the POVs felt so similar that I couldn't remember who was who (this was the case with Veradis and Kastell's early POVs that had the same feel to them and kinda blended into the same in my mind). But then as I reached the second half, I was totally sold! This read reminded me of a trek up a hill : the climb through the various obstacles is laborious and long but then you reach the top and see the beautiful and intriguing landscape spread before your eyes and before you know it, you speed the pace and find yourself running during the last miles and totally excited to reach the end of the journey ! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>But it was part of a cause. A necessary evil. Many such evils were undertaken in war, for the greater good. But it still did not sound right, hearing it said so straight and clear.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>During the last chapters, I totally understood how the slow beginning was absolutely needed to build the conclusion. It masterfully allowed <b>the characters to have a natural and meticulous development. Nothing felt rushed or forced, the last chapters flowed naturally.</b> On the other hand, something that balanced the slowness of the beginning, was the way the different POVs were arranged. Most of the chapters were pretty short and many took place months after the previous ones <b>which allowed the plot to move forward while giving short flashbacks that provided insight into what had happened in between.</b> The last 50 pages definitely moved my rating from 4 to 5 stars (I'm taking 0.5 for the slow beginning though!).<br><br>I absolutely loved the Scottish influences and the Robin Hood vibes as most of the action took place in the woods or in old fortresses and villages.<b> The characterization was brilliant and truly realistic.</b> And yes, the set is medieval, if not earlier, so yeah men were dirty and cruddy and far from glamorous! LOL. John Gwynne also created <b>a great cast of characters</b> !! My absolute favorite is Corban for now and I loved how Gwynne surrounded him with an absolutely awesome bunch of loyal friends, family members and grumpy and snarky mentors ! Corban's development and his ability to get into trouble had some Harry Potter vibes to them. It was absolutely delightful to read about him and witness the spectacular growth he gradually underwent !!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You seem to be developing a distinct talent for being in the wrong place at the wrong time."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><b>Conclusion</b><br><br>Please be patient and carry on to at least the second half of the book before deciding to DNF! <b>You will be rewarded by lots of epic action scenes and emotional and heart-wrenching situations!! </b><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Immediate reaction </u>
</b><br><br>I'm in <s>shock</s> <s>awe</s> trouble because it's 3am and I have to wake up early !<br><br>But it was totally worth it !!<br><br>Let me gather my thoughts and get some sleep and I shall come back with a review "on the morrow!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="17522848303727872309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2218782537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2218782537" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2218782537?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330545754" href="/book/show/18138300-malice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218782537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1003029039039243721">You know you’ve read a great book when you can’t stop thinking about it and imagining all the different scenarios for the next book. This book turned out way better than I thought it would, it reminds me why I love fantasy. What I love most in fantasy(epic adult fantasy to be precise) is its originality and the way the authors play at words. And this is no exception, the author use a very rare story telling style in this book. Some fantasy books starts with a bang then backstory of the main char</span>
  <span id="freeText1003029039039243721" style="display:none">You know you’ve read a great book when you can’t stop thinking about it and imagining all the different scenarios for the next book. This book turned out way better than I thought it would, it reminds me why I love fantasy. What I love most in fantasy(epic adult fantasy to be precise) is its originality and the way the authors play at words. And this is no exception, the author use a very rare story telling style in this book. Some fantasy books starts with a bang then backstory of the main character, others say a little about the Mcs backstory in the middle of the book etc, but John Gwynne started the book with the MCs as teens, how their life, family, environment is going to contribute to their future, don’t worry is not YAish, they are other MCs that are adults and lots of adults are present in the book, So that makes the beginning of the book quite slow, but since its the first book in the series its understandable. There is religion, which is a major factor in fantasy, myths, prophecies, friendship, family, politics you name them, all in this book, even with all those the action is still present with very perfectly depicted battle scenes. <br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />To say the world building is great is an understatement, the depiction is nicely done and this is a debut novel of the author. The world is really big with lots of kingdoms. I really love the writing, the book is written in third person multiple POVs of the MCs which I admit are a lot, but not up to that of Malazan, the author made it easy to understand by starting each chapter with the name of the character whose POVs is about to be read as chapter title.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />When a fantasy book has lots of characters its scary, cause that means not all of them will make it, even at that I can’t help loving them and hope the author don’t kill off all my favourites. Here is a list of my most loved and hated characters in the book.<br /><br /><b>Corban</b>, even if all the other characters die and only him survives I’ll be happy because I love him. The book started with him at 13 and ended when he turned 16. Corban acts way older than his age, he is loyal AF, his relationship with his family especially with his elder sister Cywen is so admirable. He is kind to everyone even animals, he has a pet Wolven called Storm, wolven is like a wolf but bigger and deadlier and he has one, how cool is that. Corban is also respectful and honourable.<br /><br /><b>Cywen</b> the badass knife throwing sister of Corban, she is my fav female character in the book, not because of just her love for her brother but her love and loyalty to her friends as well. Their parents really raised them well. In a world where girls are not allowed to fight her parents and brother thought her and she is putting the skill to good use.<br /><br /><b>Kastell</b> suffered more than all the characters in this book, his life has been hell growing up, even at 16 things are just getting worse for him. He is such a good person but is surrounded by pure evil. The book ended when he was 18, with him in a very bad situation, am so scared for him.<br /><br /><b>Veradis</b>, I actually liked this guy, I was rooting for him like mad but that changed when he exchanged his brain for anything Narthair says. I bet if Narthair tells him the sky is purple he will believe without arguing, he is so foolish and has stopped using his brain, I don’t hate him but if the author or anyone asks for the characters I want dead his name will be the first on the list, at list the villains have the decency to accept they are indeed evil.<br /><br /><b>Evnis</b>, to say I hate this man is an understatement, no word can do justice to how I feel about him, he is pure evil, I wish Nightblood will make an appearance and destroy him, the book started with him making a very terrible selfish decision.<br /><br />Others I love include Halion, I want more of him, Dath, Farrell, Edana and Brina.<br /><br /><u>Plot</u><br />Millennia’s ago, Elyon created a world where Humans, giants and other creatures live in peace, but that changed when Astroth another god seek to destroy the world. There was a great war, things happen and people died. Presently giants and human are enemies but manage to live in a mini harmony but now that also is changing because a prophecy is coming through and all those ancient mythical creatures are coming back. The god war between Elyon and Astroth is about to start again with humans in the middle. Both gods has picked a champion that will determine who will win the war, so everyone is preparing their army and picking a side, but politics and power drunk people are just thinking of how to get more power.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1003029039039243721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13538360703675904613">Took me a lot of time to get hang of things in this story but I really enjoyed last 25% of this book. A lot was going on from the start but author wrapped up things beautifully here. Definitely an introductory book to the great things that awaits in remaining three books.</span>

<div id="review_1809348285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809348285" />
    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46938598-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598636572p2/46938598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809348285?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/46938598-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316399739" href="/book/show/17446626-malice">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kayla by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/50812952-piera">Piera</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46938598-kayla?shelf=all-time-non-romance-faves">all-time-non-romance-faves</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46938598-kayla?shelf=br-with-devin">br-with-devin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46938598-kayla?shelf=violent-gorey-moments">violent-gorey-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46938598-kayla?shelf=2010-to-2016-releases">2010-to-2016-releases</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809348285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer382372539613143470"><a href='https://youtu.be/m8eeKwKgryw' rel='nofollow noopener'>My series review is live on my youtube channel NOW!</a><br/><br/>TRUTH AND COURAGE BITCHES<br/><br/><br/><a href='https://gracelingaccountantblog.wordpress.com/2018/09/12/book-review-malice-by-john-gwynne/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review was originally published on GracelingAccountant.</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536801913i/26294104._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Hey Ya’ll!<br/><br/>This is my spoiler free review for Malice by John Gwynne, the first book in the Faithful and the Fallen series. I buddy read this book with my friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/60582820-devin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Devin</a> and I’ve gotta say that I am obsessed with this series. I will probably be spending a good portion of OWNtober 2018 devouring at least the next book in the series. I gave this book five stars. Let’s</span>
  <span id="freeText382372539613143470" style="display:none"><a href="https://youtu.be/m8eeKwKgryw" rel="nofollow noopener">My series review is live on my youtube channel NOW!</a><br><br>TRUTH AND COURAGE BITCHES<br><br><br><a href="https://gracelingaccountantblog.wordpress.com/2018/09/12/book-review-malice-by-john-gwynne/" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally published on GracelingAccountant.</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536801913i/26294104._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hey Ya’ll!<br><br>This is my spoiler free review for Malice by John Gwynne, the first book in the Faithful and the Fallen series. I buddy read this book with my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/60582820-devin" rel="nofollow noopener">Devin</a> and I’ve gotta say that I am obsessed with this series. I will probably be spending a good portion of OWNtober 2018 devouring at least the next book in the series. I gave this book five stars. Let’s get into the review. <br><br><u>
  <b>Book Info</b>
</u><br><br>Genre(s):<br><br>Adult – Many different definitions are thrown around, but I define this as books that contain content not suitable for younger readers. This includes things like graphic content (blood, gore, torture, murder, rape), and explicit sexual content. <br><br>Epic Fantasy – Again, there are many definitions thrown around but epic fantasy is basically high fantasy (i.e. set in a completely fictional world with supernatural/mystical creatures and usually magic) but usually focused more on the life or coming of age of the main character. Often features a quest of some sort and often the main character is the “chosen one”. There is often a very strong focus on good/evil. Finally, the world is often modeled after medieval times, featuring swords, castles, dragons, horses, etc. <br><br>Page Count: 656<br><br>Release Year: 2013<br><br>Buzz Words: Chosen one, coming of age, epic fantasy, multiple POV<br><br>*NOTE: The first book is on sale through Amazon Kindle for $1.99!*<br><br><b>
  <u> My Thoughts </u>
</b><br><br>The first thing that comes to mind is just how expansive and in depth the world and characters were. There was an amazing map, and while this is usually a plus in a book, this is the first time that a book has had a map and I’ve actually found myself needing to use it. There were also a ton of POVs, more than I’ve ever read in one book (I think there were 7). This was near overwhelming when I first started reading, but eventually I started tabbing and taking notes and this really helped me early on. Here are some pictures of my copy and my notes in my journal. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536801913i/26294105._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536801913i/26294106._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536801913i/26294107._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like I said, everything being so huge and well developed was both a good thing and challenging to process. I fell in love with so many of the characters, but I also couldn’t keep the kingdoms and kings strait until I took down notes. I know not all readers, my buddy read partner included, had to do this but there was just so much to keep track of. <br><br>I was also really fascinated and surprised by the fact that the author took so much inspiration from Christian mythology, and that I actually enjoyed it. For me, the angels/demons thing is just so overdone so it’s hard to write it and still have it come across original and interesting, but Gwynne managed and I’m still shocked at how much I enjoyed it. I really appreciated that the author didn’t just go with the usual “why is he bad? because he’s bad” that many stories stick to. He really gave Asroth and the Kadoshim a history and motivations, while still tying it into the “modern day” of the story itself. <br><br>Another thing that was AMAZING was just how many possibilities the story had; this made it really easy for my buddy read partner and I to theorize about the direction of the story, which personally added to my enjoyment. I seem to have an uncanny knack for guessing plot points and character backgrounds (probably because I read so much) so it’s rare that I’m surprised about anything. I definitely guessed a few of the plot points but there were also so many surprises to the story that just blew my mind and made the book a freaking delight to read. For this reason I would definitely recommend this for a buddy read if you’re looking for something; it’s so much more fun when you have someone to bug at all hours of the day with your crazed ravings. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ There are so many examples I could give for this. Like when Corban saved that momma wolf I was just like "there is no way he doesn't somehow get a pet wolf, I just know it. Then there was the whole thing on page 376 when they found Aquilus dead I was like ooohhh how much you want to bet NATHAIR DID IT. And then when 431 rolled around I somehow just knew that Gar was one of those Jehar swordmasters that was lured away before and I was RIGHT. But even as far back as the beginning of the book when Corban touched the stone and that figure started speaking to him and the vision only ended when a white sort of light settled around his shoulders? At that point we had read that the war was going to repeat in modern day so that solidified for me that Corban was Elyon's champion so I knew when Nathair was so sure he was that he definitely wasn't. This book is nuts with the hint dropping.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>There were seven perspectives technically, but there were really only four main characters and I loved them all. Each was amazingly well developed, and each character had a major part to play in the greater picture, intertwining their stories and making it impossible to both love all the characters and be completely secure that they’ll all remain alive by the end of the story. <br><br>Corban was a sweet little boy who hadn’t yet made it to the Rowan Field (basically the right of passage to become a man, I want to say you enter at like 12 or 14?) and was incessantly bullied by a boy named Rafe who had already entered the Rowan Field. He also has a sister who seems to outshine him in the bravery department and a giant of a blacksmith father, so Corban believes he has a lot to prove. He wants to outshine everyone. He is ultimately compassionate, and brave, and protective of his family and friends and he is always looking out for those who can’t look out for themselves. On the other hand, like any child he’s hotheaded, a bit thoughtless and unconcerned about the consequences of his actions, and his desire to prove himself combines with all of this to often put him in trying and dangerous situations. <br><br>Nathair is another character in the story. Prince to Tenebral, son of Aquilus, he believes above all else that he is the best. At what, you ask? Why, everything of course. I’m joking a bit, but really his character is based on his belief that he is somehow going to be the one to make the world a better place. He believes wholeheartedly that he IS THE CHOSEN ONE and he won’t let anyone tell him different. He’s hardheaded and stubborn, and won’t do anything that wasn’t his idea. Even though his father has been King for years he has a hard time listening to him and realizing that his father makes valid points. On the other hand he is also smart, and cunning, and open-minded. He perseveres through difficulty, respects and loves the men of his warband, and no one could ever say he stands on the sidelines – he is always right there with his men fighting in the muck.<br><br>Veradis is Nathair’s first sword. Originally from Ripa, sent to Nathair to be a part of his warband and gain notoriety, his main motivation is to finally have his father be proud of him and show him the same respect his father shows his brother Krelis. He is a good man, always protective and loyal to Nathair, and would do anything Nathair asks. This unwavering loyalty is sometimes to his detriment, but he almost reveres Nathair like a person does a god. Like some kind of untouchable figure. Writing this review a couple weeks after reading the book, it’s hard to remember much else about him.<br><br>Then we have Kastell. The red – haired nephew to King Romar of Isiltir. We meet him on the road where we find out that for some unknown reason he’s been the target of his cousin Jael’s ire. When it first started it just seemed like Jael disliked him, when they were children, but it soon becomes obvious that Jael hates him to a point of wanting his life. We don’t know why, but this fued is the main focus of Kastell’s storyline. <br><br>All four of these characters have unique viewpoints, and it was really interesting to be able to actually know the thoughts of so many characters throughout the story. <br><br>One thing you really almost need warned about in this book is that nothing is what you expect it to be. I would say to pay attention really closely when you’re reading this, because the smallest things in the earlier parts of the book are actually huge clues to how the future of the book pans out. No one is safe. No lives can be guaranteed. Every character will face betrayal of a sort, and the ending is SUCH a huge cliffhanger so you should probably have the next book on hand. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean holy crap that ending was some Red Wedding next level kind of shit. No one is safe.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I chose to read this book because of a Piera Forde video that I watched and I would recommend this to anyone who loves high fantasy, or that loved Game of Thrones or Nevernight. This was one of the best books I’ve read all year and I’m so glad I have my own copies to reread over and over again.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="382372539613143470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1321719524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1321719524" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1321719524?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330545754" href="/book/show/18138300-malice">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Markus by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=put-some-brakes-on-the-hype-train">put-some-brakes-on-the-hype-train</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=the-cover-was-better-than-the-book">the-cover-was-better-than-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321719524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12893193128678820587"><i>"War eternal between the Faithful and the Fallen, infinite wrath come to the world of men. Lightbearer seeking flesh from the cauldron, to break his chains and wage the war again. Two born of blood, dust and ashes shall champion the Choices, the Darkness and Light."</i><br/><br/>See, this is quite a fun premise. A good god and a bad god will start a war, and each will have their mortal champion. Who are they, you wonder? Well, their identities are carefully hidden and you will have to work it out for yourself</span>
  <span id="freeText12893193128678820587" style="display:none"><i>"War eternal between the Faithful and the Fallen, infinite wrath come to the world of men. Lightbearer seeking flesh from the cauldron, to break his chains and wage the war again. Two born of blood, dust and ashes shall champion the Choices, the Darkness and Light."</i><br /><br />See, this is quite a fun premise. A good god and a bad god will start a war, and each will have their mortal champion. Who are they, you wonder? Well, their identities are carefully hidden and you will have to work it out for yourself...<br /><br />...so it’s a good thing that’s all fucking obvious from page one. In fact, so is everything else. Not only does this book follow a completely standard fantasy recipe (not always a bad thing), but it makes sure to spray paint the solution to every future secret revelation with huge red letters on all the walls around you (always a bad thing). <i>Malice</i> is perhaps the most predictable book I have read in the fantasy genre. There are no surprises, and every detail about how everything is going to go down, is impossible to miss.<br /><br />Except in the eyes of the characters, that is. The protagonists in this book are so pathetically, monumentally, unreasonably, unrealistically moronic and naive that everything gets past them. And so you’re left sitting waiting for the painfully obvious to catch them unawares. Yes, they’re young and stupid. Yes, they don’t have all the information. There are many excuses one could make, and none of them even come close to mitigating these examples of cataclysmic idiocy (there is one scene in particular I will always remember from this book, which is unfortunately an example of just this). But alas, when the whole world is too obvious for comfort, the characters in it have to be kept in the dark even when it makes no sense, so that the storyline can go where it clearly must go.<br /><br />It is also striking that all the young male main protagonists are so similar they might as well have been called Bob 1, Bob 2 and Bob 3. Maybe even Bob 4, depending on who and how you count.<br /><br />There are quite a few interesting supporting characters to begin with. And in impressive ways, they almost without exception all manage to lose their appeal. Mostly that is because you start realising that they are <b>all</b> cardboard cutouts only functioning as plot devices placed somewhere for the furtherance of the author’s plan. Just like the protagonists, that is. And then one of the two that remain somewhat interesting at the end turns out to be a secret bastard prince, taking his trope-ridden archetype factor to level 437.<br /><br />The writing and the worldbuilding are the best parts of the book, as they are somewhat adequate if you’re being very generous. In fact, there are quite a few decent aspects here. But literally everything <i>Malice</i> attempts to do, has been done so much better elsewhere.<br /><br />How on earth did it come to this conclusion? Based on the number of positive reviews, I started reading the book expecting at least a fantastically fun reading experience, if not a masterpiece, and for the first third of the book I thought that was what I was getting. Sure, the writing was not particularly impressive, but it was genuinely enjoyable and a real page-turner, and I thought the rather uninteresting protagonists were just uninteresting because it was early on and they were going to develop. I thought the prologue was spectacular because I thought it was going to actually be important. I thought there would be great twists, great fights, and great fun.<br /><br />Then the glaring flaws kicked in so fast and hard that I felt mistreated as a reader.<br /><br />Look, there is potential in this thing. It could have been so much better. And all this said, I am still somewhat intrigued by what happens next, so I might read the second book. At least some of the characters now know who the bad guys are, I think. Mostly because the bad guys have killed their friends and loved ones in front of them. Maybe that will have made them see it?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12893193128678820587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16686652341462602364" style="display:none">Malice (The Faithful and the Fallen, #1), John Gwynne<br /><br />Young Corban watches enviously as boys become warriors under King Brenin’s rule, learning the art of war. <div id="review_1811025803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1811025803" />
    <a title="Holden Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21469231-holden-johnson"><img alt="Holden Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573691309p2/21469231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1811025803?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holden Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holden Johnson" href="/user/show/21469231-holden-johnson">Holden Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18888122-malice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21469231-holden-johnson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21469231-holden-johnson?shelf=grimdark-fantasy">grimdark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21469231-holden-johnson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811025803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9837100503611161429">Holy...<br/><br/>What an ending. It's almost as if John Gwynne is begging me to buy book two...<br/>Oh wait, I already did.<br/><br/>A quick note before I get into the review:<br/><br/>I feel as if this series was written for me. In my mind, me and John Gwynne met up for coffee and he asked me what I loved about fantasy books and I wrote a list for him on a napkin and he then took it and wrote a book about it.<br/><br/>I will have two sections to this review. The Non-Spoilery version which will come first and the Super-Duper-Spoilery versi</span>
  <span id="freeText9837100503611161429" style="display:none">Holy...<br /><br />What an ending. It's almost as if John Gwynne is begging me to buy book two...<br />Oh wait, I already did.<br /><br />A quick note before I get into the review:<br /><br />I feel as if this series was written for me. In my mind, me and John Gwynne met up for coffee and he asked me what I loved about fantasy books and I wrote a list for him on a napkin and he then took it and wrote a book about it.<br /><br />I will have two sections to this review. The Non-Spoilery version which will come first and the Super-Duper-Spoilery version which will come last. I will scream and shout when that is about to happen so that you don't accidentally wander into unknown regions of this review.<br /><br />In John Gwynne's debut novel, Malice, we encounter many different things that any lover of fantasy, rpgs, dungeons and dragons, video games, etc will love.<br /><br />Magical artifacts(weapons) of untold power.<br />Hidden and mysterious races and civilizations.<br />Betrayal<br />Intrigue<br />Coming-of-age tales<br />Family bonds<br />Awesome beasts/animals<br />Training and "leveling-up"<br /><br />These may be odd descriptions for what you will find in Malice, however as an avid gamer(of both video and board games), I find specific things stick out to me more and bring me more enjoyment when reading books. <br /><br />I love when characters grow and you see progression in them. On that note, however, I hate when characters second guess themselves the entire time about their progression. This did not happen in Malice and I was sooooo thankful. When a character learns something, or makes progress, they take it and run with it. By the end of Malice everyone has changed, for the better or worse, but they have.<br /><br />I've really grown to love the type of pacing and quick chapter style that this sort of writing brings. I'm constantly telling myself, "Just another chapter. My kindle only says 5 minutes. That's easy." As someone with limited time, due to work and many other hobbies, I find this incentive a refreshing take on fantasy. I've read many (MANY) novels with 40 pages per chapter of describing clothing and scenery. While there is a time and place for these, and some are just fantastically done and paced really well, I find more often than not I devour John Gwynne's type of writing/pacing much easier and it is much more enjoyable. The quote-on-quote boring parts are short, as Gwynne trusts his readers to be intelligent enough to fill in the minor gaps in detail. We are smart. Our brains don't need to know every detail of a blade of grass. We want the juicy stuff and bloody fights! I'd ask for more of those, but got plenty in Malice. Plus, I'm positive more are coming shortly xD.<br /><br />As a debut novel, you can definitely see some rough edges at the beginning of Malice. As the pages turn and the story progresses, John Gwynne really hits his stride and shakes off the awkwardness in an amazingly short amount of time. By the end of Malice, you'd expect John Gwynne to have written scores of books and that this is just another one of his amazing works to top a grand stack of them.<br /><br />At first, I had no problem turning the pages, though I wasn't enthralled. By the end I want to spend time in real life with most of the characters and am going to write letter after letter to John Gwynne begging him not to kill them. (Too bad all of the books in the series are out already =( )<br /><br />Okay, now comes the spoilery discussion<br /><br /><br /><br />YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED. PLEASE TURN BACK IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THIS BOOK.<br /><br /><br /><br />LAST CHANCE.<br /><br /><br /><br />DANGER.<br /><br />Okay, I no longer feel sorry if you read on.<br /><br /><i>‘Being called a fool and being treated as a fool are two entirely different things, my dear,’</i><br /><br />These are in random order because it's late and my brain is all crazy from that ending.<br /><br /><b>Corban</b> - Yay Corban! Let's start off with the awesome lad. I want to begin by mentioning that awesome duel at the end verses Rafe (Who I hate with a passion at this point). The avid-fantasy-reader in me expected him to lose the duel, rather by trickery or his fear overcoming him. This scene showed exactly what I look for in a novel. Growth. Corban took out Rafe like it was nobodies business. That put a big smile on my face.<br /><br />Corban and his family have such a strong bond that you can't NOT feel for them. You feel part of the family when reading Malice. Gwynne does a great job of showing the importance of family. I love how Corban takes every task head on. Sure, sometimes he doesn't think about the decisions he makes, but he uses his gut. That is the opposite of manipulation, which Nathair does exclusively. I'd take Corban any day of the week. I wish him best of luck in the remaining books. He will need it.<br /><br /><i>Both the brave man and the coward feel the same. The only difference between them is that the brave man faces his fear, does not run.’</i><br /><br /><b>Veradis</b> - At first Veradis was one of my favorite character. He has an attractive personality, is sharp-witted, and deadly with a blade. He rises through the ranks to first-sword quickly. I have high hopes for him and hope that he sees through the shroud that is Nathair. He seems a just person, but keeps rationalizing with himself that what he is doing is right. We've seen this weakness in humans all of the time, and unfortunately I think it will take some big event to change him.<br /><br /><i>You will be the anvil, I the hammer</i><br /><br /><b>Nathair</b><br />I hate you manipulative jerk. At the beginning it was hard not to side with the ambitious young lad. But by the end you could almost see the manipulative hand of Asroth on his shoulder, even before Corban could actually see it. Nathair's story shows spot on how someone can be manipulated and led slowly into their own destruction, believing it was their decision and plan the whole time. Gwynne wrote this very well, in my opinion. He's not a POV character, but I had to write about him.<br /><br /><i>‘Empire . . .’ he breathed. ‘There must be an empire. This land needs to be united and strong if we are to be ready when Asroth comes. That will never happen while the Banished Lands are governed by a score of bickering children. An empire, with an army such as the ants we saw, that fights together as one to defeat any foe in its way. I will make Father see this truth. Out of the ashes of his old dream a new one shall be born, and I will give my life to see it come to pass.’</i><br /><br /><b>Cywen</b><br />I believe that she's still alive. I have hopes for her becoming a strong warrior someday, as her skills with throwing knives are top notch. Her pride in Corban makes me happy, as I have three sisters of my own. Once again, her family bond makes me happy.<br /><br /><b>Evnis</b><br />At first, I felt for this guy. His wife died. The king pretty much was a big part of that. I wasn't too mad at him, but by the end, you know that he is twisted. I don't hate him s much as Nathair, and can possibly, maybe see a redemption story for him? But we will have to wait and see.<br /><br /><b>Kastell / Maquin</b><br />How could I not tie these two together? The ending left an opening for Kastell to either be dead, or still kicking, but he was a great character. Maybe not the most interesting at times, but as a duo, I loved every minute of the chapters they were in. Maybe I'm just a sucker for dynamic duos.<br /><br /><b>Camlin</b><br />My favorite type of character. Loyal to no one but himself, but still somehow can't stop doing the right thing. He's a good guy and though misguided, I see a great future ahead for him. Plus, he's pretty funny.<br /><br />I think there might be another or two? Not sure.<br /><br />The supporting cast is all amazingly well done. Every character has a reality to them that is hard to come by with such a large cast. Gwynne makes the reader care about every single one of them, at least to some degree.<br /><br />RIP my friends =(<br /><br />Current theories/Theories I had before I sign off:<br /><br />Corban - Bright Star<br />Nathair - Black Sun<br />Random Hammer in Corban's Dad's house - Treasure? It was mentioned twice very specifically.<br />Caldius - One of Asroth's demons<br /><br />I'd recommend this book for any nerdy fantasy fan, regardless of the medium they enjoy it in. Malice is a great debut novel and book in general. I am so excited to delve into book two starting...<br /><br />now.<br /><br />Thanks ^_^<br /><br />-Holden<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9837100503611161429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1921422910057027000">The only big regret I have while reading this book was reading it for three months straight. Am absolutely glad I was able to complete it cause it was absolutely worth it.<br/><br/> This first book is a little bit a coming of age story, which was quite interesting. I was able to witness the characters develop in and also in other skills.<br/><br/><i>
  <b> ‘Be very sure you mean the words that come out of your mouth. You cannot unsay them.’</b>

  <span id="freeText1921422910057027000" style="display:none">The only big regret I have while reading this book was reading it for three months straight. Am absolutely glad I was able to complete it cause it was absolutely worth it.<br /><br /> This first book is a little bit a coming of age story, which was quite interesting. I was able to witness the characters develop in and also in other skills.<br /><br /><i>
  <b> ‘Be very sure you mean the words that come out of your mouth. You cannot unsay them.’</b>
</i><br /><br />The plot centres on an angel and demon war but in a fantasy setting. I truly can't wait to see what unfolds in the next book.<br /><br /><b>World Building And Writing </b><br />The world building was great, there was a lot of travelling in this book but not the boring kind. This helped to show other kingdoms and their culture. This book is very rich in culture, tradition also history. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />The characters definitely made this book so much better. I can't imagine this book with different characters.<br />	Corban; I love the person he's growing up to be. His character development was so amazing, can't wait to see what the future holds for him.<br />	Nathair; All I do is imagine him in a <s>skirt </s>kilt. I found him to be quite okay at first but then he started making some decisions I didn't appreciate.<br />	Veradis; I believe him to be a very loyal dog. I felt like he didn't have enough of a personality and he was convenient for just Nathair.<br />	Cywen; She's an amazing character and I can’t wait to see her rise to her full potential in the next book.<br /><br />There are a bunch of other characters but I won't go into detail about them now. Can't wait to find out what happens in the next book.<br /><br /><br /></span>
